Talks

Where to Settle Down?

— Tianli

"Chinese people are unfortunate Chinese people." This seems to be a pre-"destined" fate. Just look around: those living in border areas are bombed by enemies, and those living abroad are "expelled" (the wealthy are naturally excluded).

Recently, we have seen "bandit suppression" victory reports, Sichuan war news, and the retreat of North China's anti-Japanese troops to "pre-determined defense lines" in the newspapers. However, it is also worth noting that over four thousand overseas Chinese in Mexico have been deported back to China, and more than twenty thousand are expected to return eventually. In the eyes of the great and powerful, this is naturally a trivial matter. After all, if you lose your homeland, you can still live in "villas" abroad and will never be "expelled." Not only will you not be expelled, but you will also be treated as a "state guest."

The "unfortunate fate" of Chinese people seems to have been "destined" for a very long time. It is not something that has only been plucked from a three-stringed instrument recently. Let's ignore the four hundred million or so "A Dou" (a derogatory term for someone incompetent) in the country who are fortunate enough to sit in "cars" (referring to those in power) and not care where the "driver" (the government) will take them. Let's calculate how many years of "tomb luck" (bad luck) the one thousand one hundred thirty-three thousand five hundred (according to a 1932 survey by the Central Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission) "refugee Chinese" have already gone through, and how many more years they have to go.

In a society that values settling down, with no assistance from the government, simply to escape natural and man-made persecution, overseas migration has created the great achievement of "ten million" people. Unexpectedly, we have been given the honor of being second only to Norway. However, these ten million heroic pioneers of our nation have endured great hardship and undergone rigorous selection. In the process of migration, relying solely on natural struggles, the old and weak who were not suitable were mostly eliminated. Those who made it to the forefront were all outstanding individuals. The successful result is the remittance of tens of millions of yuan back to the motherland each year. Under special circumstances, there were even "patriotic donations." Consequently, the central government established an agency specifically for receiving donations from overseas Chinese.

But the "unfortunate fate" of Chinese people is ultimately "destined." If you do not have "British" or "American" citizenship, then this "unfortunate fate" will cover you both at home and abroad. Those living abroad can expect to be beaten by foreigners' whips and guns. The massacres of overseas Chinese in Southeast Asia by the Spanish on several occasions are well-known historical facts. And the two massacres during the Tokyo earthquake and the Korean riots are still fresh in our memories. Because of the global economic recession, the last straw is always broken on the backs of Chinese people. The expulsion of overseas Chinese and the refusal of Chinese laborers to disembark have become common news items in daily newspapers. And what about our government? Aside from a diplomatic document in foreign affairs, all that remains is a message of condolence for these warriors who have been defeated in the national economy. The wise government has the opportunity to send special envoys to explain the "anti-foreign" rumors to foreign bigwigs, but has no time to argue about the fact that overseas Chinese are being "rejected."

Now, we can still retreat to "pre-determined defense lines" in military affairs, but what about the economy? There is no defense line to defend. The state of a semi-colonial economy is more depressed than that of a colony. Therefore, these pioneers of the national economy, who have been forced to retreat, have no room for activity in the stagnant atmosphere of the motherland.

The Emerald Ring

— Yingdai

Teacher X, who has never spoken Chinese and only speaks English in the classroom, has obviously lived abroad for too many years, so he can't speak Chinese! He speaks English very fluently, and he also uses English to annotate the names of all the students in the class when he takes attendance, which shows that he cannot read Chinese characters. Yet he is indeed Chinese.

Usually, in the classroom, he treats the male students with a stern face, but he always has a kind of smile that he dares not overdo with the female students. Perhaps this is his respect for women and disregard for men, and he has his own unique views and purposes? No wonder the male students are angry and do not like him!

How strange! One day, when he came to class, he was suddenly seen wearing an emerald ring on his hand; there is nothing strange about wearing a ring, but what is strange is that this ring was worn on the index finger of his left hand. As a result, it attracted the attention of all the male and female students in the class. In our knowledge of love and pursuit, we all know that wearing a ring on the index finger indicates that one is unmarried and is in the process of pursuing the opposite sex, so unnecessary thoughts naturally swirl in everyone's minds, perhaps because of the impulse of curiosity or the burning of jealousy?

"Doesn't he have a wife yet? He looks like he's around forty years old."

"There must be a reason why he's wearing an emerald ring on his index finger today!"

"We should pay attention to him and investigate the truth!"

"Is he thinking about our Angel?"

"Looking at him, he doesn't look like a weasel trying to eat swan meat! No way!"

Because of the discovery of this emerald ring, no one could hear what he was saying in this class. From beginning to end, the students' gazes were all focused on his ring. Some were silently thinking, and some were discussing in whispers, all their attention focused on the ring problem.

When he walked into the classroom, the first female student to spot his emerald ring was suspicious of him and told the other female students, and then all the female students paid attention to his ring, as if the purpose was to wear it for them.

After class that day, the male and female students had a big discussion, and everyone's face was filled with resentment. Nameless jealousy was burning hotly in the hearts of the male students.

"Damn it! There must be a reason for his ring today."

"Ah! He's going to pull this kind of performance!"

"We should guard against him!"

"According to my reason, our female students will never be seduced by him!"

"That's not necessarily a foregone conclusion!"

"I knew he wasn't a good thing!"

"Bastard! He's also pursuing our..."!

The above is the discussion of the male students after class. That day, the male students went to the dormitory and no one was in the mood to read or study on their own, and they were just discussing this issue.

At the same time, in the girls' dormitory, they were also chatting like this...

"His ring naturally means that he is not engaged."

"It is said that he went abroad from a young age, so he can't speak Chinese. Maybe it's because he was abroad that he hasn't married yet."

"He looks three parts like a ghost and seven parts like a human. Who would want to marry him!"

"If he wears this ring again next class, I won't go to class!"

"What does he take us for!"

"He just wants to...us!"

"It's really outrageous!"

"A ghostly face, he's too overestimating himself!"

The conversations in the girls' dormitory that day spread to the ears of the male students the next day, and people's hearts settled down a lot. Everyone was saying...

"Our female students are all very knowledgeable!"

"Everyone is sacred and inviolable!"

"He's just wasting his efforts! Haha!"

What is Life?

"What is life?" This question often swirls in my mind like a whirlwind.

I remember not long ago, I once had such a discussion with a friend. Because this friend was newly immersed in the sea of love, he firmly believed that life was all about love.

"What exactly do we seem to be born into this world for?" I asked him.

"Ha! Your question has a very rich philosophical color!" He couldn't help but laugh; but then he answered me with a serious face; "You may not believe what I say; not only you, you can say that all those who have not been involved in love will not believe it! Do you think it's too intense? No! I absolutely believe in the phrase 'Love is a sacred medicine'. What career? What creation? These are all lies. Do you think so? For example, life is a body, and love is the soul; without the soul, there is no intention to manage any great career. So I say that life is all about love!"

"Then, when you wake up from your dream, you may laugh at today's thoughts."

So we stopped talking about this issue.

Another time. I remember raising this elusive and unanswerable question with another friend. However, the result was to replace love with "money"; the reason was to believe in the four words "money is omnipotent". Of course, this did not satisfy me; however. Apart from these two answers, no one told me a third new answer. Therefore, I still blindly lived in the world all day long.

However, I believe, and I believe with all my heart; life is definitely not just about pursuing money and love. In the future, something that contains a great comforting power will be born on earth, its power can break a dozen boring lives, and create unlimited light! At this time, guns and cannons have been abolished, the world has been united, and all people live in peace, without quarrels or disputes, but I don't know if we have the blessing...

This is just my dream! The question "What is life?" still swirls in my mind like a whirlwind all day long!

Literary Arts

— Jinzhi

Fallen Flowers

It is truly pitiful that crushed jade buries fragrance;

Empty branches face the clear smoke by themselves.

Since ancient times, beauties have found it hard to have long lives;

Do not blame Heaven for being heartless.

From the beginning, a flower's fate is delicate and thin;

Outside the curtains, its fluttering flight strains the eyes to see.

A thousand years of regret flow in the water of three lifetimes;

Empty pavilions face the setting sun, slanting.

A garden full of vibrant purples and charming reds,

Has sent away several fits of madness and outdated customs.

In the end, splendor is but a dream;

Turning the head, wealth and rank have already become empty.

On branches, red flowers are seen for only a few days;

Blooming, fading, flourishing, and withering all belong to the Creator.

The world's splendor is inherently like this,

No need to feel melancholy and blame the east wind.

Good Omens

— Sick Horse

An English newspaper argues that China may yield to Japan, but the spirit of the people cannot be suppressed, proving that the responsibility for national downfall does not lie with the people.

The authorities in Peiping are unwilling to acknowledge compromise? After the Japanese secretary Mr. Nakayama visited Mr. He and Mr. Huang, an important meeting was held, resulting in the necessity of a response visit!

This year is the Year of National Products. National products are selling well. Although the customs import tax rate has not decreased, revenue is booming.

Sales of aviation lottery tickets are enthusiastic. In the future, they will be improved, and the ticket price will be reduced so that ordinary people have the purchasing power and do not miss the opportunity to make a fortune.

Mr. Lu Buyi, 27 years old, from Wuxi, has worked as a primary and secondary school teacher, principal, factory traveling salesman, and bookkeeper. He is proficient in Chinese, arithmetic, and calligraphy. He is now willing to take on the above positions at a monthly salary of 25 yuan or more. Correspondence address: No. 73, Zhoujia Arch, Songpan Road, Yangshupu, Shanghai. Mr. Du XX, has worked for a certain construction company and is now willing to work as a pattern maker for various construction companies or as a pen drawing trainee for various advertising companies. Remuneration is not a concern. Correspondence address: c/o Mr. Wang Shixiong, Xinfu Construction Company, No. G4, Shenyu, Tiantong Road.

Shop Assistant Correspondence

Serving as an Accomplice to a Tiger

To the Editor:

I am a junior staff member of a large candy company on Nanjing Road in this city and now request that you answer the following questions.

Today, the company's senior executives (directors) held secret discussions to build a residence for the general manager, whom they described as hardworking and meritorious. The funds for this will be forcibly borne by the staff and workers of the company's main store and branches in this city and other locations, as well as the factory. Each person will have one-tenth of their salary deducted each month for a period of five months. Mr. Editor, what are your thoughts on this news?

It is pitiful that we laborers have already sold our entire bodies and minds like commodities; what we receive is only enough to maintain life. Now, these so-called magnates, heartless and disregarding the lives of others, still cruelly devise ways to plunder us. Mr. Editor, how should we deal with this!

The struggle of one person is powerless, so I want to unite and stand on a single battle line to resist. However, we usually have no organization, and it is not easy to suddenly come together to deal with this already occurring event. Mr. Editor! Should we submit? Should we resist? I am hesitating!

In this situation, I want to state the reasons why I cannot afford it to the directors on the one hand, and explain the advantages and disadvantages of this move to the general manager and request that he find a way to stop it; but they are colluding with each other. Mr. Editor! Do you have a solution? I eagerly await a reply. Sincerely, Xu Shangda.

Editor's note: "Reading Mr. Xu's letter makes one hate the capitalists' henchmen who serve as accomplices to tigers. In many situations, we can often see that the capitalists themselves, although their hearts cannot be questioned, still have some concerns on the surface and dare not act recklessly in every way. Only these henchmen, because they want to fulfill their dream of being promoted to capitalists, flatter the capitalists wholeheartedly; on the one hand, they use their authority to exploit the laborers; on the other hand, they send signals to the capitalists. As a result, the laborers are indeed the first to bear the brunt and be slaughtered; but the capitalists, if they are not careful, create a huge storm, lose big for small, like a dog eating pork lard wrapped in bamboo bows, unable to explain themselves. Therefore, this kind of scum is simply a pest of society, and simply a fuse for labor-capital disputes. I regret that I have no power, otherwise I would definitely send one of them to the guillotine. Dear laborers! In your struggle, they are your first targets; as long as these people exist, don't even think about having a good day. Wise capitalists! Don't think that they are your loyal servants, their motives are entirely for themselves; once something goes wrong, they can shirk responsibility! Quickly see through their treacherous schemes, quickly drive them away. Then, in China, where production is backward, you will have your place, otherwise, I am afraid you will become the target of public criticism.

Therefore, we strongly support Mr. Xu's desire to appeal to the manager; but we believe that it is unnecessary to state your case to the directors, as it is useless and harmful to seek skin from a tiger. Rise up and attack these objects together.

Novel

The Life of the Five Geishas (21) (Continued)

— Ling Hong

Eighteen · Autumn

Time flies so quickly, in the blink of an eye, it's autumn again.

Our Miss Liu is indeed a sentimental poet. She leans by the window, gazing at the ginkgo tree stretching over the wall, almost scorched yellow, quietly listening to the autumn wind sweeping through the treetops, and inevitably feels the icy coolness on her body. If cold rain were added, she would inevitably paint a bleak picture in her inspiration. So she involuntarily hums the line "The autumn wind and autumn rain make one sad." From this, it can be seen that Miss Liu has indeed increased her knowledge a lot in recent years.

Minister Su Gengyun has been in a really good mood lately, and today he pestered her for a long time again. Now, seeing Miss Liu standing by the window in a daze, he can't help but tiptoe up behind her, put his hands on her shoulders, and say in a low voice...

"Why are you standing here silently? Are you thinking about something again?"

"Thinking about something? Don't make me laugh. I'm not some high-ranking official, and I don't need to worry about national affairs. What worries could I have?"

"You're mocking me again, you sharp-tongued girl. But you need to know that national affairs and the worries of young ladies are not the same, and national affairs don't need you to care about. But the worries of young ladies are always heavy, cherishing people in the scenery, composing poems about the wind and moon, these are naturally the elegant and romantic affairs that are a young woman's duty. But I don't know which person you're thinking about right now?"

Because he mentioned this, the heroic figure of Zhang Wenbin immediately surfaced in her mind, so she couldn't help but twist her mouth and say...

"Is there any need to ask? Of course, I'm thinking about you."

"Thank you, but I don't think you're really that kind. I'm afraid you're thinking about that big guy, Gu..."

"Bah! How can you say that?"

"That's what you say, but I always feel a little uneasy. Hey, let me tell you something serious, would you officially marry me?"

"Marry you?" Miss Liu really found it a bit funny. "Are you really saying that? But don't you already have four, including your first wife? Isn't that enough?"

"You can't say that. Let me tell you; for example, my wife, you know, she's already old, and besides playing a few rounds of mahjong, she can't do anything. A woman being old is indeed not a big deal. The second one is Japanese, and she has to personally handle a lot of correspondence, and she's busy from morning till night, so there's no fun in the bedroom. The third one, to be honest: she comes from a humble background and can only accompany me to sleep. The fourth one goes without saying, she's too young and doesn't understand anything, and sometimes she cries for her mother behind my back, which is really ridiculous. And my two daughters are all grown up now, and their mother is worried about them and won't let them go to a girls' school to study, so they still have little education and don't know how to socialize, so they'll inevitably be unable to stand their ground in society in the future. So I often think like this; if you could come to my house, that would be great. Not only would my daughters be able to be educated, but even I, the old man, would be able to sit with you all day long, chatting and laughing, which would be the happiest thing."

"What a flirtatious old man, I didn't expect you to be in such a good mood." Miss Liu couldn't help but laugh loudly; "But how do you know that I have to marry you?"

"How can you say that? If you were a little more loving to me, then I think..."

Miss Liu laughed again. Before long, the twilight of autumn had quietly crept up again.

Film Special

From the Song "Spring River Flower Moon Night" to Emerging Music (Part 1)

— Ren Xida

The music in "Spring River Flower Moon Night" (Tell me tonight) mostly adopts important parts from two Italian operas, Boheme (by Puccini, 1858-1924) and Rigoletto (by Verdi, 1813-1901), and cinematicizes them in terms of performance form, rather than bringing the entire stage opera to the screen.

But why, in this year of 1930-something, would we still be enamored with songs from the 1880s? It's best to first discuss the development of music in the last decade.

Although "jazz" music had already flowed from black people into the so-called civilized United States before the European War, after this so-called civilized United States industrialized this primitive music, the inherent dance music of Europe and the United States, One step, advanced into the current Foxtrot. However, due to the outbreak of the European War, people in society were living in deep water, so this kind of dance music had no chance to become popular. After the European War, American industry gradually developed, and "jazz" also developed with the development of industry. After 1924, the economy of Europe also gradually showed prosperity, and the power of "jazz" therefore penetrated into Europe.

Each era must have the art of each era. The industrial era will inevitably produce music that praises and exaggerates the power of machines. "Jazz" was born in this era, so the characteristic of "jazz" music is that it is "organized" and relatively "popular." Later, because of the deeper development of capitalism, the form of "jazz" music also advanced from "Foxtrot" to "Samba," whose characteristic is to completely describe the sound of train movements. However, this kind of pure mechanical sound is ultimately too simple in musical form. It is not enough to express the prosperity of capitalism. So "Charleston," "Black Bottom"... various forms followed. The ambition of this kind of tune is to "mechanize" all things in the universe, animals, and human movements, to show the greatness of machine power! So when "jazz" music at this time really entered a state of madness, the entire European and American society was anesthetized by this bourgeois music, especially the petty bourgeoisie, who were even more severely anesthetized. Many music students and composers took "jazz" as a career, and naturally "jazz" became "commercialized" and lost its artistic value. At the same time, since "jazz" had penetrated into the petty bourgeoisie, most of the "jazz" gradually became "petty bourgeois." However, despite this, the bourgeois musical characteristics of "jazz" still exist strongly. Until 1926, this bourgeois "jazz" music was called the peak flowering period.

From 1927 to 1928, although machines were still developing vigorously, capitalists were showing serious crises in industry and economy, and their status was gradually shaken. Then this kind of music representing the "flowering era" of capitalism is of course not suitable for the era of current society. So this kind of declining, sad "Blues" and passive, sentimental "Tango" tunes developed gradually in response to the times, and were able to suit the emotions of the times and penetrate into the psychology of ordinary people in society. It occupies a considerable position in the development process of "jazz" music. (To be continued)

Film Reviews

Review of "Broadway Bad"

— Yan Nan

Walking out of the Nanjing Grand Theater, what surfaced in my mind was the directing technique of "Broadway Bad." Indeed, this film is devoid of interest in terms of meaning and performance. Only the exquisite and transcendent art is worth savoring.

The plot of this film is very simple... It tells the story of a showgirl who is about to marry a rich man, but unexpectedly has a falling out with him due to a temporary misunderstanding, and she falls in love with a director in the dance troupe. Later, the rich man takes the four-year-old child born to the showgirl as his own and sues her in court. After the showgirl vehemently defends herself, the court's verdict still awards the child to the showgirl, and the case ends, and the script ends inexplicably.

The film is titled "Broadway Bad," but there is no love in the content, only carnal desire, only the love of mother and child, the showgirl's vehement explanation of everything is only for her son, and she is not moved at all by her old lover, the rich man. At the same time, the film does not describe anything about the personalities of the rich man and the dance troupe director, the two male protagonists. Of course, all their actions are sudden in the eyes of a third party. How did the rich man fall in love with the showgirl in the first place? The director uses money as a stepping stone for courtship. The character and personality of both of them make people extremely suspicious. Joan Blondell, who plays the showgirl, is very good, especially at the end, her tearful, bitter smile leaves an unforgettable impression on people, and her other emotions such as surprise, joy, anger, and false smiles are also very moving. She is the only focus of the whole film, and the other characters are bland and unremarkable. The male lead, Ricardo Cortez, is usually a very good actor, but here he is so stiff, he can only be called a "handsome wooden man."

The scenery is very unique, and the angle of the camera makes it feel very beautiful. The lighting is also very good, and close-ups (special shots), medium shots, and long shots each have their own charms. Many of the borrowed special shots are extremely humorous. The on-screen explanations are clever and commendable.

The director is the only hero of the film. He knows how to be clever and win the audience's laughter. Although many places are to avoid difficulties and take the easy way, and are lazy, it is not annoying, but feels pleasantly convoluted, and small interludes are his proud forte. For example, describing the intimate shape of a pair of lovers, he uses a blown piece of paper to describe it, and he uses the human head of the brass knocker on the door to compare the hideousness of the rich man's face. These are all places that make the audience yearn for it. The organization is deliberately scattered, and then a clue is found from a tangled mess, making people clap their hands and exclaim in admiration.

If you are an art lover, then this film is quite suitable for your needs, especially film industry workers should go and see it.

Review of "Humanity"

— Ling He

If we do not deny the sophistication of American film performance techniques (although these techniques are only suitable for their own ideologies), then the performance of "Humanity" is worth boasting about.

The director has a deep consideration of the old Montage, so in terms of mood, it is indeed very compact from Dr. Mao's treatment of the girl in danger, all the way to Ead. Of course, this is the focus of the play, and the first half is just a necessary accompaniment, so the director narrates it with short shots, but it is not too loose. However, in the back, that kind of quiet and beautiful picture and tense air are the result of the director's hard work. The most noteworthy is when the girl is in the emergency room. Two more children and a dog are added to stare beside her, making this tense picture vivid, from which it can be seen the director's painstaking efforts. He is also very attentive to all small occasions, such as blocking the light with a newspaper in front of the poor man's sickbed. He is even very particular about lighting and scenery. In short, the director is very successful.

Regarding the performance, of course, both Dr. Mao and his son have their own achievements. Ralph Morgan, who plays the father, has a full grasp of the personality of "Humanity," and the true feelings of a loyal and kind elder are revealed in every move. However, his facial expressions are always lacking, for example, when the detective arrives, he can only express his nervousness in his tone. As for the two female roles, they are both mediocre, and the one who plays the doctor's assistant is not very skilled.

However, this film has a significant shortcoming, that is, the old doctor dies too quickly and strangely. This is the fault of the director and screenwriter, and strictly speaking, it is unreasonable. However, we should not have too much extravagance for this kind of film.

As for meaning, this kind of film is very opportunistic for the real society. A good doctor must empathize with the poor and sick with a compassionate heart, which is considered to be loyal to his profession. As for the law, of course, it must be obeyed, so the young doctor repents after committing a heinous crime. Because of this, the selfless law can not hold him accountable. That's all.

New Film Preview

Movie Stars Enjoy Poor Life

— Bing

Because of the increasing number of thieves in Hollywood recently, Hollywood movie stars store all their property in the bank to avoid accidents, and they have to use temporary checks to withdraw money, so one day they were invited to enjoy the life of poor boys.

This day, American banks encountered a special holiday, and all the banks in the country were closed, and the banks in Hollywood also took a day off. In the morning, the newspapers in Hollywood were delivered to the homes of the stars, and the big headline on the newspaper read that the banks would be closed today. Several stars with empty pockets were all complaining. Hollywood became a poor world on this day, and many stars frowned.

Al Jolson happened to have no money in his pocket, and immediately borrowed money from a rich friend. Jack Oakie was so anxious this day that he almost couldn't afford breakfast. Shevley happened to run out of gas in his car and borrowed two dollars from his servant to buy gasoline. Stuart Owen couldn't borrow money and went home to steal his child's piggy bank. Panghor Hokins came out in a car, but he didn't have a dime on him. Later, he ran to Paramount, and a gatekeeper at Paramount happened to have received his salary a day earlier and had a few dollars left, so he lent it to her. Ginger Rogers couldn't even pay off her six-dollar and nine-cent debt. Lily and Hismen dumped out all the money in their wallets, and there was only one dollar and three cents. Roland Young went to eat, but he didn't have any money. Fortunately, he was familiar with the restaurant, so he wrote an account and ate a meal on credit for a day. Dawi Mannar also had only two dimes and seven cents left in her wallet. The newly arrived British star in Hollywood, Weila Angie, didn't know that American banks would be closed on this day, and didn't withdraw money in advance, so she was also empty-handed. There were also Zoling Crili, Eileen Deng, and Gary Croft, etc., whose meals were included in the hotel, so they didn't have to pay in cash, but small accounts were required. On this day, they all wrote IOUs to the waiters.

Zhejiang Grand Theater's Aviation Dance

In addition to showing Pescaden's "Photography King," the Zhejiang Grand Theater specially hired a full class of dancers to perform various new-style dances, and in order to promote aviation to save the country, a "Aviation Dance" section was added. During the performance, airplanes rise and fall, the national flag flutters, and the words "Aviation to Save the Country" are written in large characters, which is both timely and can promote the patriotic thinking of the Chinese people.

Overview of Soviet Russian Films (2)

— Written by Rudolf Messner, Translated by Bao Han

In Russia, film is regarded as one of the most important parts of an all-encompassing plan for ideological education. The so-called ideological education is the education within the communist philosophy. The Soviets have realized the great power of film in education. Therefore, whether it is on the lips of young women or in the people's congress, every time the word film is mentioned, there is a solemn and dignified declaration. What these Soviet women or congressmen have realized is no different from what our country's young women or congressmen have also realized; what is different is that the Soviets have taken strict steps to preserve the educational power hidden within film, so that it is not covered by other things, which is what people inside and outside our country's lower house have not yet had time to consider.

Within the Soviet Union, the so-called education is of course a matter that is very synonymous with propaganda. Since the facts are like this, it is not surprising that we can see that the products of the Soviet Russian film production studios and the films shown in cinemas are nothing but propaganda films. (The import of foreign films will be discussed separately later)

It is our European custom to walk into a magnificent theater, and to seek a fun of entertainment and relaxation under the dim silver light, so when we suddenly encounter this harsh attitude, we are easily amazed. Just imagine, if there is no Laurel and Hardy, no foot of the Western wilderness, no sight of Tesduri galloping in the gravel, and even Garbo is not seen, what will become of this scene? Only propaganda, propaganda, and what is the meaning of propaganda? Europeans who enter Soviet Russia will ask in bewilderment, "Where shall I go to seek some light entertainment?" Russians will be able to tell you without hesitation, "In the circus! In the dance hall! In the park for educational recreation! You can seek it wherever you go. If you want to seek entertainment in the cinema, that is just wishful thinking."

Because in the minds of the Soviets, the propaganda power of film is extremely important and must not be allowed to fall into decline, or to diminish its strength in empty and meaningless entertainment. And the Russians may also ask you, "Is it true that our propaganda films have no entertainment value at all?" In fact, the best films such as "The Golden Mountains" also have quite a bit of entertainment to be found; the next best ones such as "The Black Black Skin" are not necessarily so; and then descending to third-rate films such as The Quiet Don, there is absolutely none (to be continued)
